# Excalidraw Data

## Text Elements
A (Police Officer): We believe these new rules will help crime prevention. First, CCTV cameras are installed to cover the whole town. They help monitor public areas. Second, identity cards are checked by police in spot checks to identify individuals. Third, phone calls can be monitored by the authorities to find criminals. Fourth, social networks are monitored to keep track of dangerous plans. Fifth, teenagers' phones are registered on GPS systems so their location is stored. Sixth, number plate cameras on roads act as a deterrent to crime. All this information is stored to keep everyone safe. ^BV0ys14o

B (Parent): As a parent, I have mixed feelings. I agree that CCTV cameras are needed for safety; they help crime prevention. Police checking identity cards is okay if it is done respectfully. But monitoring phone calls? That feels like an invasion of privacy; too much personal data is accessed. Monitoring social media is also worrying; my child's information is stored without their full understanding. Registering teens' phones on GPS is good for their safety, I can know where they are. Number plate cameras on roads are fine if they only keep track of criminals. My main worry is how this data is used. ^vVZDOtgB

C (Teenager): I think most of this is an invasion of privacy. CCTV cameras everywhere mean we are monitored all the time. Police checking our ID is scary. Monitoring phone calls and social media is wrong; our private conversations are accessed by the authorities. Forcing GPS on our phones means our location is stored and tracked always, not just by parents but by police. Only the number plate cameras might be okay if they only catch criminals, but I don't trust it. All this surveillance technology means our freedom is taken away. We feel like suspects, not people. ^xxej0rgn

#English ^ZdjWUZAd
